Jamison Brereton

94 (920)
Pressing Stones
The snake Arbuda K─Бdraveya
14 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 5, 7, 14
This second hymn to the pressing stones (for the relations among the three press ing-stone hymns, see the introduction to X.76) is a playful and imaginative praise of these implements for extracting the soma juice from the plant. The stones are animatized throughoutтАФas human workers, as hungry bulls, as birds, as antelopes, as horses. But there is special emphasis on them as speakers. The first four verses begin with тАЬspeakingтАЭ verbs (and often continue with them), with a variant phrase beginning verse 5, and the last two verses (13тАУ14) echo these verbs. These last two verses treat the unhitching of the stones, their task completed, and the last p─Бda of verse 14 rather poignantly not only releases them but de-animatizes them: they are now perceived as just stones.

рдПрддреЗ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рдг рдЙрдкрд▓рд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░ рд╡рджрдиреНрддреБ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд╡рд╢рдмреНрджрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреБ ред рд╡рдпрдВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╡рджрджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд╡рд╢рдмреНрджрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рднреНрдпрдГ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡реНрдгрд╛рдорд░реНрдерд╛рдп рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рдкреНрд░ рд╡рджрд╛рдо ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рд╣реЗ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬреЛ рдпреВрдпрдордкрд┐ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рд╡рджрдд рдкрдардд ред рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рдЕрджреНрд░рдпрдГ рдЖрджрд░рдгреАрдпрд╛ рджреГрдврд╛рдГ рдЖрд╢рд╡рдГ рд╕реЛрдорд╛рднрд┐рд╖рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгрдГ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рдГ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рдгрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╕рд╛рдХрдВ рд╕рд╣ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдердВ рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХрдВ рд╢реНрд░реЛрддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдШреЛрд╖рдореН рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд╡рд╢рдмреНрджрдВ рднрд░рде рдкреЛрд╖рдпрде рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рд╕реЛрдорд┐рдирдГ рд╕реЛрдорд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реЛрдореЗрди рддреГрдкреНрддрд╛ рднрд╡рде рее ред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet these (stones) speak; let us reply to the speaking stones, and do you (priests) utter (praise); when,you solid, quick-moving stones, you utter the noise of praise together to Indra, (then you become) full of theSoma.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let them speak forth; let us speak forth. Speak a speech to the pressing stones that are speaking,
when, o stones, o mountains, all together you swift ones possessed of soma bear your signal-call, your cry to Indra.

Griffith

LET these speak loudly forth; let us speak out aloud: to the loud speaking Pressing-stones address the speech;
When, rich with Soma juice, Stones of the mountain, ye, united, swift to Indra bring the sound of praise.

Geldner

Diese sollen ihre Rede anheben, wir wollen unsere Rede anheben. Haltet eine Rede auf die redenden Steine, wann ihr Felsen, ihr Berge, des Soma┬┤s voll zusammen rasch euer taktm├д├Яiges Ger├дusch f├╝r Indra erhebet!

Grassmann

Sie sollen singen, wir auch wollen singen nun; den Steinen singet euer Lied, den singenden, Wenn ihr gewalt’ge, schnelle Felsen im Verein dem Indra Soma bringend Sang und Klang erhebt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey roar like a hundred, like a thousand (men); they cry aloud with green-tinted faces; obtaining thesacrifice, the pious stones through their piety partake of the sacrificial food, even before (Agni), the invoker (ofthe gods).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They speak as if in hundreds, in thousands. They roar with their golden mouths.
Having toiled at their good work, the good workers, the stones, have achieved the eating of the oblation even before the Hotar.

Griffith

They speak out like a hundred, like a thousand men: they cry aloud to us with their green-tinted mouths,
While, pious Stones, they ply their task with piety, and, even before the Hotar, taste the offered food.

Geldner

Diese reden hundertf├дltig, tausendf├дltig, sie br├╝llen her mit ihren gelben M├дulern. Da die Steine t├дtig waren, Gutes wirkend mit gutem Werke, sind sie noch vor dem Hotri zum Genu├Я des Opfers gelangt.

Grassmann

Es singen diese hundertfach und tausendfach, mit gelben M├дulern wiehern sie entgegen uns, Die Steine emsig m├╝hend sich mit frommem Werk, sind fr├╝her als der Priester selbst zum Mahl gelangt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey speak, they received into their mouth the sweet (Soma), they roar (like the eaters of flesh) overthe roasted meat; chewing the branch of the purplle tree, the voracious bulls have bellowed.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They speak; in this way they found the honey. They growl over the cooked flesh.
Gnawing at the branch of the reddish tree, the gluttonous bulls have
bellowed out to it.

Griffith

Loudly they speak, for they have found the savoury meath: they make a humming sound over the meat prepared.
As they devour the branch of the Red-coloured Tree, these, the well-pastured Bulls, have uttered bellowings.

Geldner

Diese reden, sie haben dabei die S├╝├Яigkeit gefunden. Sie schlampfen ├╝ber dem gargekochten Fleische. Indem sie nach dem Zweige des r├╢tlichen Baumes schnappen, haben die gutkauenden Stiere dabei losgebr├╝llt.

Grassmann

Sie singen, denn sie fanden nun den s├╝ssen Trank, sie brummen l├╝stern bei dem gar gewordnen Fleisch, Des rothen Strauches Zweig zerkauend haben jetzt die Stiere, die so viel verschlingen, laut gebr├╝llt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey cry aloud calling upon Indra with the intoxicating effused (Soma), they took the sweet Soma intotheir mouth, seized by the sister (fingers) the bold stones danced, filling the earth with shouts.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They speak loftily by reason of the delighting delightful (soma).
Shrieking to Indra, in this way they found the honey.
(Fit) to be clasped by the sisters [=fingers], the clever ones have danced, making the earth heed with their trampling.

Griffith

They cry aloud, with strong exhilarating drink, calling on Indra now, for they have found the meath.
Bold, with the sisters they have danced, embraced by them, making the earth reecho with their ringing sound.

Geldner

Sie reden laut, durch den berauschenden, lustigmachenden Soma berauscht, den Indra anschreiend haben sie dabei die S├╝├Яigkeit gefunden. Kundig haben sie mit den Schwestern untergefa├Яt getanzt, mit ihrem Getrappel die Erde widerhallend machend.

Grassmann

Sie singen kr├дftig mit dem Trank, der sie berauscht, nach Indra rufend, denn sie fanden schon den Meth; Nun tanzen sie umschlungen von der Schwesterschar mit Kunst, sodass die Erde dr├╢hnt von ihrem Schall.

рд╕реБрдкрд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ рд╕реБрдкрддрдирд╛ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рдгрдГ рдЙрдк рдЙрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдп рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ рджреНрдпрд╡рд┐ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдореН рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд╡рд╢рдмреНрджрдореН рдЕрдХреНрд░рдд рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдЖрдЦрд░реЗ ред рдореГрдЧрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╡реНрд░рдЬ рдЖрдЦрд░рдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдЗрд╖рд┐рд░рд╛рдГ рдЧрдордирд╢реАрд▓рд╛рдГ рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛рдГ рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрдореГрдЧрд╛ рдЗрд╡ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рддрдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╡рдЪреНрдЫреНрд╡реЗрддрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛ рджреНрд░рдкреНрд╕рд╛рдГ рдЕрдирд░реНрддрд┐рд╖реБрдГ рдиреГрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдирд┐рд╖реНрдХреГрддрдВ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рднрд┐: рдкреАрдбрд┐рддрдВ рд╕рддреН рдЙрдкрд░рд╕реНрдп рдЙрдкрд▓рд╕реНрдп рдиреНрдпрдХреН рдЕрдзреЛрдореБрдЦрдВ рд╕реЛрдордВ рдирд┐ рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдирд┐рдЧрдордпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдкреБрд░ рдмрд╣реБ рд░реЗрддрдГ рд╕реЛрдорд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдореБрджрдХрдВ рджрдзрд┐рд░реЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рее рее реиреп рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe well-gliding stones made a noise in the firmament; they danced (like) the black deer in the stall;they exude down from the upper stone the expressed (Soma); white as the sun they yield abundant moisture.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The eagles have raised their speech up to heaven. In their lair the black antelopes have danced vigorously. Down they go downward to the rendezvous with the lower one. They have themselves produced much semen from the sun-bright one.

Griffith

The Eagles have sent forth their cry aloft in heaven; in the sky’s vault the dark impetuous ones have danced.
Then downward to the nether stone’s fixt place they sink, and, splendid as the Sun, effuse their copious stream.

Geldner

Die Adler haben ihre Stimme gen Himmel erhoben, die schwarzen Antilopen haben eifrig auf dem Weideplatz getanzt. Sie gehen nieder zum Besuch des unteren Steins; sie lassen reichlich den Samen des sonnenhellen Soma.

Grassmann

Zum Himmel schallt der schnellen V├╢gel lauter Sang, die muntern Rehe tanzen in der H├╢hle nun; Sie gehn herab ins Brautgemach des untern Steins, die sonnenhellen lassen vielen Samen dort.

рд╡реГрд╖рдгрдГ ред рдлрд▓рдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реГрд╖рд╛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдГред рддрд╕реНрдп рдзреБрд░рдГ рдзреБрд░рдВ рднрд╛рд░рдВ рдмрд┐рднреНрд░рддрдГ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрдд рдПрддреЗ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рдгрдГ ред рд╕рд╛рдХрдВ рд╕реЛрдореЗрди рд╕рд╣ рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд╣рдиреНрддрдГ рд░рдердВ рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдг рд╡реЛрдврд╛рд░рдГ рдЙрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдЙрджреНрдЧреВрд░реНрдгрд╛ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рдЗрд╡ рд╕рдорд╛рдпрдореБрдГ рд╕рдорд╛рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЖрдпрддрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рд╢реНрд╡рд╕рдиреНрддрдГ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд╡рд╕рдордп рдЙрддреНрдкрддрдирдирд┐рдкрддрдирд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрд╛рд░рдЬрдирд┐рддреЗрди рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдирд╛ рд╢реНрд╡рд╕рдиреНрдд рдЗрд╡ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╛ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рдгрдГ рдЬрдЧреНрд░рд╕рд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╕реЛрдордВ рдЧреНрд░рд╕рдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдЕрд░рд╛рд╡рд┐рд╖реБрдГ рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рдпрдиреНрддреЗ рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдореН рдПрд╖рд╛рдВ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡реНрдгрд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреА рдкреНрд░реЛрдердердГ рдореБрдЦрд╛рдЪреНрдЫрдмреНрджрдГ рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡реЗ рд╢реНрд░реВрдпрддреЗ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рдЕрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рдорд┐рд╡ ред рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдиреЛ рдореБрдЦрд╛рджреНрдзреЗрд╖рд╛рд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рдпрдерд╛ рддрджреНрд╡рджрд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBearing the burden of the sacrifice, yoked with (the Soma), they extend themselves like spiritedhorses; when panting and extracting (the Soma), they cried aloud, their snoring is heard like that of horses.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Like powerful draft(-horses), they have held fast, yoked together, the bulls bearing the chariot-poles.
When panting and gulping they have bellowed, their snorting sounds like that of chargers.

Griffith

Like strong ones drawing, they have put forth all their strength: the Bulls, harnessed together, bear the chariot-poles.
When they have bellowed, panting, swallowing their food, the sound of their loud snorting is like that of steeds.

Geldner

Wie starke Zugtiere im Fahren ziehen sie an, zusammen eingespannt, die Stiere, die die Joche tragen. Wenn sie keuchend, schlingend gebr├╝llt haben, so h├╢rt sich ihr Schnauben wie das der Rennpferde an.

Grassmann

Wie starke Rosse fahrend ziehn die Str├дnge sie, zugleich geschirrt die Stiere, tragend gleiches Joch; Wenn schnaubend, fressend sie erheben ihr Gebr├╝ll, dann klingt es wie Gewieher einer Rosseschar.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWorship (priests), those imperishable (stones) which have ten workers, ten girths, ten yokes, tenagents, ten encompassers, which are possessed of ten burdens, which bear (the sacrifice).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The ten workersetc., are the ten fingers; Nirukta 3.9

Jamison Brereton

To those who possess ten tracks, ten girthbands, ten yoking cords, ten yokes,
ten reinsтАФsing to the unaging ones pulling ten chariot-poles, ten yoked ones [=fingers?].

Griffith

To these who have ten workers and a tenfold girth, to these who have ten yoke-straps and ten binding thongs,
To these who bear ten reins, the eternal, sing ye praise, to these who bear ten car-poles, ten when they are yoked.

Geldner

Lobsinget den Steinen, die zehn ……, zehn Gurte, zehn Str├дnge, zehn Geschirre, zehn Z├╝gel haben, die nie altern, die zehn Joche, die zehn angejochten Finger ziehen.

Grassmann

Singt denen, die der Bahnen und der Gurte zehn, die zehn der Str├дnge haben, zehnfach angeschirrt, Die nimmer altern, durch der Z├дume zehn gelenkt und die zehn Deichsel, zehn verbundne Joche ziehn.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese stones, having ten reins, swiftly moving, their delightful whirling goes round; they first tasted theambrosia of the fragment of food of the expressed Soma.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These swift stones have ten fastening straps. Their delightful harness encircles (them).
They have taken as their share the beestings of the pressed somian stalk of the first plant.

Griffith

These Stones with ten conductors, rapid in their course, with lovely revolution travel round and round.
They have been first to drink the flowing Soma juice, first to enjoy the milky fluid of the stalk.

Geldner

Die Steine sind Renner mit zehn Riemen, ihr Zaun legt sich angenehm herum. Sie haben vom ausgepre├Яten somischen Trank den Seim des ersten Stengels genossen

Grassmann

Zehnfach gez├дumten Rossen sind die Steine gleich, und ihre Fahrt uml├дuft den lieben Somatrank; Des besten Stengels erste Milch genossen sie, des ausgepressten Somakrautes besten Trank.

рд╕реЛрдорд╛рджрдГ рд╕реЛрдорд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреНрддрд╛рд░рдГ рддреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд╛ рдПрддреЗ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рдгрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╣рд░реА рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реМ рдирд┐рдВрд╕рддреЗ рдирд┐рдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддрд┐ рдЪреБрдореНрдмрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдЧрд╡рд┐ рдЕрдзрд┐рд╖рд╡рдгрдЪрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рдЕрдВрд╢реБ рд╕реЛрдордВ рджреБрд╣рдиреНрддрдГ рдЖрд╕рддреЗред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рддреЗрднрд┐рдГ рддреИрдГ рджреБрдЧреНрдзрдВ рд╕реЛрдореНрдпрдВ рд╕реЛрдордордпрдВ рдордзреБ рдЕрдореГрддрдВ рдкрдкрд┐рд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкреАрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд░реНрдзрддреЗ рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд╢рд░реАрд░реЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдкреНрд░рдерддреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгрд╢рд░реАрд░рд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рд╡реГрд╖рд╛рдпрддреЗ рд╡реГрд╖реЗрд╡рд╛рдЪрд░рддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese devourers of Soma kiss Indra’s horses, milking forth the juice they repose upon the cow, Indrahaving quaffed the sweet Soma milked forth by them increases, waxes broad, grows vigour.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The soma-eaters kiss the two fallow bays of Indra. Milking the plant, they sit on the cow(hide).
Having drunk the somian honey milked by them, Indra grows strong, spreads out, plays the bull.

Griffith

These Soma-eaters kiss Indra’s Bay-coloured Steeds: draining. the stalk they sit upon the ox’s hide.
Indra, when he hath drunk Soma-nicath drawn by them, waxes in strength, is famed, is mighty as a Bull.

Geldner

Diese Somaesser k├╝ssen Indra┬┤s Falbenpaar; indem sie die Stengel ausmelken, sitzen sie auf der Stierhaut. Wann Indra das von ihnen ausgemolkene somische S├╝├Я getrunken hat, w├дchst er, geht er in die Breite, f├╝hlt er sich als Bulle.

Grassmann

Die Somafresser gr├╝ssen Indra’s Rossepaar, die Pflanze melkend sitzen dort sie bei der Kuh; Wenn Indra trinkt den Methsaft, den sie ausgemelkt, so wird er gross und breit und kr├дftig wie ein Stier.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Soma is your showerer (at the sacrifice); you are unharmed, (like those) abounding in food, youare constantly feeding; like the wealthy (possessed) of splendour, you, O stones, are beautiful (at the sacrifice ofhim) whose sacrifice you delighted in.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your plant is a bull. You will certainly not suffer harm. You are always possessed of nourishment, (well-)fed.
You are pleasing to him whose ceremony you have enjoyed because of your grandeur, as if because of a richly endowed (daughter, given to him in marriage?), o pressing stones.

Griffith

Strong is your stalk; ye, verily, never shall be harmed; ye have refreshment, ye are ever satisfied.
Fair are ye, as it were, through splendour of his wealth, his in whose sacrifice, O Stones, ye find delight.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSplitting, but unsplit, you, O stones, are untiring, unrelaxing, immortal, free from disease, undecaying,rising and falling, powerful, unthirsting, not genitive rating thirst.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Drilled or undrilled, you stones are unwearying, unslackened,
immortal,
unailing, unaging, unbudgeable, very stout, unthirsty, unthirsting.

Griffith

Bored deep, but not pierced through with holes, are ye, O Stones, not loosened, never weary, and exempt from death,
Eternal, undiseased, moving in sundry ways, unthirsting, full of fatness, void of all desire.

рд╣реЗ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рдгрдГ рдпреБрдЧреЗрдпреБрдЧреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рдпреБрдЧреЗрд╖реБ рдзреБрд╡рд╛ рдПрд╡ рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд▓рд╛ рдПрд╡ рд╡рдГ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдкрд┐рддрд░рдГ рдкрд┐рддреГрднреВрддрд╛рдГ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рдГ рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд╛рдорд╛рд╕рдГ рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд╛рдорд╛рдГ рд╕рджрд╕рдГ рд╕рджрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рдЖрддреНрдордирд╛ рди рдпреБрдЮреНрдЬрддреЗ рди рд╕рдВрдпреЛрдЬрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ред рдЕрдЬреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рд╕рдГ рдЬрд░рд╛рд░рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдГ рд╣рд░рд┐рд╖рд╛рдЪрдГ рд╕реЛрдорд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрднрдХреНрддрд╛рд░рдГ рд╣рд░рд┐рджреНрд░рд╡рдГ рд╕реЛрдорд╕рдВрд╕рд░реНрдЧрд╛рджреНрдзрд░рд┐рддрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ рджреНрдпрд╛рдВ рджрд┐рд╡рдВ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдВ рдЪ рд░рд╡реЗрдг рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд╡рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рдЕрд╢реБрд╢реНрд░рд╡реБрдГ рд╢реНрд░рд╛рд╡рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour progenitors (the mountains), stable from age to age, desirous of repose, seek not to mix with(religious) assemblies; exempt from decay, enjoying the Soma, flowing green (with Soma), they made heavenand earth resound with their clamour.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Firmly fixed are your fathers [=mountains] in every age. Desirous of repose, they do not hitch themselves up from their seat.
Undecaying, companions of the golden (soma), (like) golden trees, they have made Heaven and Earth listen by their bellowing.

Griffith

Your fathers, verily, stand firm from age to age: they, loving rest, are not dissevered from their seat.
Untouched by time, ne’er lacking green plants and green trees, they with their voice have caused the heavens and earth to hear.

Geldner

Ganz unbeweglich sind eure V├дter zu aller Zeit, Ruhe liebend fahren sie nicht von ihrem Platz weg. Nicht alternd, die Gef├дhrten des gelben Soma, Gelbholz, machten sie durch ihr Get├╢se Himmel und Erde aufhorchen.

Grassmann

Fest stehn die Berge, eure V├дter, immerdar, die Ruhe liebend gehn sie nicht von ihrem Platz; Ihr, ewig jung, zum goldnen eilend liebevoll habt Erd und Himmel nun erf├╝llt mit eurem Schall.

рдЕрджреНрд░рдпрдГ рдЖрджрд░рдгреАрдпрд╛ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рдгрдГ рдпрд╛рдордиреН рдпрд╛рдордирд┐ рдЧрдордиреЗ рдЕрдЮреНрдЬрд╕реНрдкрд╛рдГ ред рдЕрдЮреНрдЬрд╕рд╛ рдкрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрдЮреНрдЬрд╕реНрдкрд╛рдГред рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд░рдерд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдЗрд╡ рдЙрдкрдмреНрджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рддрджрд┐рддреН рддрджреЗрд╡рд╛рднрд┐рд╖рд╡рдХрд░реНрдо рд╡рд┐рдореЛрдЪрдиреЗ рдШреЗрддреН рддрддреН рд╕реЛрдорд░рд╕рд╡рд┐рдореЛрдЪрдирд╡реЗрд▓рд╛рдпрд╛рдордкрд┐ рд╡рджрдиреНрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдмрдкреНрд╕рддрдГ рд╕реЛрдордВ рднрдХреНрд╖рдпрдиреНрдд рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛рдг: рд╡рдкрдиреНрддрдГ “рдзрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛рдХреГрддрдГ рдХреГрд╖реАрд╡рд▓рд╛: рдмреАрдЬрдорд┐рд╡ рдпрдерд╛ рдкреГрдЮреНрдЪрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рд╕реЛрдордВ рдкреГрдЮреНрдЪрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╕рдВрдкрд░реНрдЪрдпрдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рди рдПрдирдВ рдорд┐рдирдиреНрддрд┐ ред рди рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe stones proclaim it with their clamour at the issue of the Soma, like the quick-protecting (chariots)on the road; like cultivators sowing the seed, they, devouring the Soma, mix it, and do not hurt it.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just so do the stones speak at their unhitching, *or on their course they speak with their tramplingsтАФthe stones as they drink (the soma)
directly.
Like grain-producers [=farmers/millstones] strewing seed, strewing
their тАЬseedтАЭ [=semen] they engorge the soma. They do not diminish
him though they gnaw at him.

Griffith

This, this the Stones proclaim, what time they are disjoined, and when with ringing sounds they move and drink the balm.
Like tillers of the ground when they are sowing seed, they mix the Soma, nor, devouring, minish it.

Geldner

Dasselbe sprechen die Steine bei der Ausspannung und auf der Fahrt mit ihrem Getrappel, dem Geklapper, die gleichsam unmittelbar trinken. Wie Kornbauende den Samen ausstreuend mehren sie den Soma, nicht mindern sie ihn schl├╝rfend.

Grassmann

So singen bei der Einkehr sie und auf der Fahrt, mit lautem L├дrm die Steine Somatrinkern gleich, Und f├╝llen gleich dem Landmann, der den Samen streut, den Soma ein, doch fressend mindern sie ihn nicht.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(The Soma) being effused at the sacrifice, they made a noise like (children) at plural y, striking theirmother. Proclaim the praise of (the stone), which has effused (the Soma), let the honoured stones revolve.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When (the soma) was pressed in the ceremony they raised their voice, like playful (boys) jostling their mother.
Unhitch (the stones) that have pressed it and release the inspired
thought of the (priest) who has pressed it. Let them roll away, being (now) perceived as (just) stones [/the stones no longer being held in
harness].

Griffith

They have raised high their voice for juice, for sacrifice, striking the Mother earth as though they danced thereon.
So loose thou too his thought who hath effused the sap, and let the Stones which we are honouring be disjoined.

Geldner

Bei dem ausgepre├Яten Opfer haben sie ihre Stimme erhoben, wie spielende Kinder die Mutter sto├Яend. L├╢se fein den dichterischen Gedanken des, der ausgepre├Яt hat! Sie sollen jetzt abtreten, sich als Steine f├╝hlend!

Grassmann

Beim Opfersafte haben lustig sie geschrien, die Mutter stossend wie beim Spiel die Kinder; Mach, Soma, frei des Kelterers Gebete, die hehren Steine m├╢gen rings sich tummeln.
